<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Diddylogo.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Diddylogo.png/225px-Diddylogo.png" decoding="async" width="225" height="91" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/99/Diddylogo.png 1.5x" data-file-width="293" data-file-height="118" /></a></span></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Sean Love Combs</b> (born <b>Sean John Combs</b>; November 4, 1969), also known by his <a href="/wiki/Stage_name" title="Stage name">stage names</a> <b>Puff Daddy</b>, <b>Puffy</b>, <b>P. Diddy</b>, or <b>Diddy</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Allmusic_Bio_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic_Bio-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> is an American rapper, record producer, record executive and actor. Born in <a href="/wiki/Harlem" title="Harlem">Harlem</a>, Combs worked as a talent director at <a href="/wiki/Uptown_Records" title="Uptown Records">Uptown Records</a> before founding his own record label, <a href="/wiki/Bad_Boy_Records" title="Bad Boy Records">Bad Boy Records</a>, in 1993. Combs has produced and cultivated artists such as <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">the Notorious B.I.G.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Usher_(musician)" title="Usher (musician)">Usher</a>.
</p><p>Combs' debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/No_Way_Out_(Puff_Daddy_album)" title="No Way Out (Puff Daddy album)">No Way Out</a></i> (1997), has been certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">seven times platinum</a>. The album was followed by <i><a href="/wiki/Forever_(Puff_Daddy_album)" title="Forever (Puff Daddy album)">Forever</a></i> (1999), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Saga_Continues..." title="The Saga Continues...">The Saga Continues...</a></i> (2001), and <i><a href="/wiki/Press_Play_(album)" title="Press Play (album)">Press Play</a></i> (2006), all of which were commercially successful. In 2009, Combs created and produced the musical group <a href="/wiki/Diddy_%E2%80%93_Dirty_Money" title="Diddy – Dirty Money">Diddy – Dirty Money</a>; they released their successful debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Last_Train_to_Paris" title="Last Train to Paris">Last Train to Paris</a></i> in 2010. His fifth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Love_Album:_Off_the_Grid" title="The Love Album: Off the Grid">The Love Album: Off the Grid</a></i>, was released in September 2023.
</p><p>Combs has won three <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a> and two <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Video Music Award">MTV Video Music Awards</a> and is the producer of <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Making_the_Band" title="Making the Band">Making the Band</a></i>. In 1998, Combs founded the clothing retailer <a href="/wiki/Sean_John" title="Sean John">Sean John</a>. He was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Fashion_Designers_of_America" title="Council of Fashion Designers of America">Council of Fashion Designers of America</a> award for Menswear Designer of the Year in 2000 and won in 2004. He has been the <a href="/wiki/Brand_ambassador" title="Brand ambassador">brand ambassador</a> for vodka retailer <a href="/wiki/C%C3%AEroc" title="Cîroc">Cîroc</a> since 2007, and co-founded the television network and news website <a href="/wiki/Revolt_(TV_network)" title="Revolt (TV network)">Revolt</a> in 2013. In 2022, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> estimated his <a href="/wiki/Net_worth" title="Net worth">net worth</a> at US$1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Sean John Combs was born in the <a href="/wiki/Harlem" title="Harlem">Harlem</a> neighborhood of New York City on November 4, 1969. Raised in <a href="/wiki/Mount_Vernon,_New_York" title="Mount Vernon, New York">Mount Vernon, New York</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-New_York_Magazine_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_Magazine-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> his mother Janice Combs (née Smalls) was a model and teacher's assistant,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201013,_16_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201013,_16-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and his father, Melvin Earl Combs, served in the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Air_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Air Force">U.S. Air Force</a> and was an associate of convicted New York drug dealer <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lucas_(drug_dealer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Frank Lucas (drug dealer)">Frank Lucas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-New_York_Magazine_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_Magazine-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-roots_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roots-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> At age 33, Melvin was shot to death while sitting in his car on <a href="/wiki/Central_Park_West" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Park West">Central Park West</a>, when Sean was two years old.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201014_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201014-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Combs graduated from <a href="/wiki/Mount_Saint_Michael_Academy" title="Mount Saint Michael Academy">Mount Saint Michael Academy</a> in 1987. He played <a href="/wiki/Gridiron_football" title="Gridiron football">football</a> for the academy, and his team won a division title in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-Gangland_News_June_2005_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gangland_News_June_2005-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Combs said he was given the nickname "Puff" as a child, because he would "huff and puff" when he was angry.<sup id="cite_ref-USA_Today_August_2005_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USA_Today_August_2005-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Combs was a business major at <a href="/wiki/Howard_University" title="Howard University">Howard University</a> but left after his sophomore year.<sup id="cite_ref-Andrews_2014_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Andrews_2014-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, he returned to Howard University to receive an Honorary Doctorate in Humanities and to deliver the University's 146th Commencement Address.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-5_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-5-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="1990.E2.80.931996:_Career_beginnings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1990–1996:_Career_beginnings">1990–1996: Career beginnings</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Bad-boy-ww.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bad-boy-ww.jpg/220px-Bad-boy-ww.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bad-boy-ww.jpg/330px-Bad-boy-ww.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bad-boy-ww.jpg/440px-Bad-boy-ww.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2960" data-file-height="2236" /></a><figcaption>Bad Boy headquarters on <a href="/wiki/Broadway_(Manhattan)" title="Broadway (Manhattan)">Broadway</a> near <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a>. A billboard of Combs is in the distance.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Combs became an <a href="/wiki/Intern" class="mw-redirect" title="Intern">intern</a> at New York's <a href="/wiki/Uptown_Records" title="Uptown Records">Uptown Records</a> in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201023_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201023-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-YNUptown_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YNUptown-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> While working as a talent director at Uptown, he helped develop <a href="/wiki/Jodeci" title="Jodeci">Jodeci</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-grabow.biz_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grabow.biz-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In his college days Combs had a reputation for throwing parties, some of which attracted up to a thousand participants.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201024_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201024-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In 1991, Combs promoted an AIDS fundraiser with <a href="/wiki/Heavy_D" title="Heavy D">Heavy D</a> held at the <a href="/wiki/City_College_of_New_York" title="City College of New York">City College of New York</a> (CCNY) gymnasium, following a charity basketball game. The event was oversold, and a <a href="/wiki/City_College_stampede" title="City College stampede">stampede occurred in which nine people died</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201024–25_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201024–25-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1993, after being fired from Uptown, Combs established his new label <a href="/wiki/Bad_Boy_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Bad Boy Entertainment">Bad Boy Entertainment</a> as a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Arista_Records" title="Arista Records">Arista Records</a>, taking then-newcomer Christopher Wallace, better known as <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">the Notorious B.I.G.</a>, with him.<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Black_Profile_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Black_Profile-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Both Wallace and <a href="/wiki/Craig_Mack" title="Craig Mack">Craig Mack</a> quickly released hit singles, followed by successful LPs, particularly Wallace's <i><a href="/wiki/Ready_to_Die" title="Ready to Die">Ready to Die</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Combs signed more acts to Bad Boy, including <a href="/wiki/Carl_Thomas_(singer)" title="Carl Thomas (singer)">Carl Thomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faith_Evans" title="Faith Evans">Faith Evans</a>, <a href="/wiki/112_(band)" title="112 (band)">112</a>, <a href="/wiki/Total_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Total (band)">Total</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201049_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201049-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Father_MC" title="Father MC">Father MC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DJ_Booth_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DJ_Booth-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The Hitmen, his in-house production team, worked with <a href="/wiki/Jodeci" title="Jodeci">Jodeci</a>, Mary J. Blige, <a href="/wiki/Usher_(musician)" title="Usher (musician)">Usher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lil%27_Kim" title="Lil&#39; Kim">Lil' Kim</a>, <a href="/wiki/TLC_(group)" title="TLC (group)">TLC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boyz_II_Men" title="Boyz II Men">Boyz II Men</a>, <a href="/wiki/SWV" title="SWV">SWV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">Aretha Franklin</a>, and others.<sup id="cite_ref-iTunes_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iTunes-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mase" title="Mase">Mase</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Lox" title="The Lox">the Lox</a> joined Bad Boy just as a widely publicized rivalry with the West Coast's <a href="/wiki/Death_Row_Records" title="Death Row Records">Death Row Records</a> was beginning. Combs and Wallace were criticized and parodied by <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">Tupac Shakur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suge_Knight" title="Suge Knight">Suge Knight</a> in songs and interviews during the mid-1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201052–53_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201052–53-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> During 1994–1995, Combs produced several songs for TLC's <i><a href="/wiki/CrazySexyCool" title="CrazySexyCool">CrazySexyCool</a></i>, which finished the decade as number 25 on Billboard's list of top pop albums of the decade.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_1999_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_1999-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison201128_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison201128-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1997.E2.80.931998:_.22Puff_Daddy.22_and_No_Way_Out"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1997–1998:_&quot;Puff_Daddy&quot;_and_No_Way_Out">1997–1998: "Puff Daddy" and <i>No Way Out</i></span></h3>
<p>In 1997, under the name Puff Daddy, Combs recorded his first commercial vocal work as a rapper. His debut single, "<a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Nobody_Hold_Me_Down" title="Can&#39;t Nobody Hold Me Down">Can't Nobody Hold Me Down</a>", spent 28 weeks on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart, peaking at number one.<sup id="cite_ref-Hot_100_1997-03-22_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hot_100_1997-03-22-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> His debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/No_Way_Out_(Puff_Daddy_album)" title="No Way Out (Puff Daddy album)">No Way Out</a></i>, was released on July 22, 1997,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> through Bad Boy Records. Originally titled <i>Hell up in Harlem</i>, the album underwent several changes after <a href="/wiki/Murder_of_Christopher_Wallace" class="mw-redirect" title="Murder of Christopher Wallace">the Notorious B.I.G. was killed</a> on March 9, 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-xxlmag_2007_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxlmag_2007-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Several of the label's artists made guest appearances on the album. <i>No Way Out</i> was a significant success, particularly in the United States, where it reached number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> in its first week of release, selling 561,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201063_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201063-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The album produced five singles: "<a href="/wiki/I%27ll_Be_Missing_You" title="I&#39;ll Be Missing You">I'll Be Missing You</a>", a tribute to the Notorious B.I.G., was the first rap song to debut at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100; it remained at the top of the chart for eleven consecutive weeks and topped several other charts worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201061_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201061-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Four other singles&#160;– "Can't Nobody Hold Me Down", "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_All_About_the_Benjamins" title="It&#39;s All About the Benjamins">It's All About the Benjamins</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Been_Around_the_World" title="Been Around the World">Been Around the World</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Victory_(Puff_Daddy_song)" title="Victory (Puff Daddy song)">Victory</a>"&#160;– were also released. Combs collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Page" title="Jimmy Page">Jimmy Page</a> on the song "<a href="/wiki/Come_with_Me_(Puff_Daddy_song)" title="Come with Me (Puff Daddy song)">Come with Me</a>" for the 1998 film <i><a href="/wiki/Godzilla_(1998_film)" title="Godzilla (1998 film)">Godzilla</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Come_with_Me_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Come_with_Me-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The album earned Combs five nominations at the <a href="/wiki/40th_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="40th Grammy Awards">40th Grammy Awards</a> in 1998, and would go on to win the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Grammy Award for Best Rap Album</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rock_on_the_Net_1998_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rock_on_the_Net_1998-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201072_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201072-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> On September 7, 2000, the album was certified septuple platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> for sales of over 7 million copies.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, Combs was sued for landlord neglect by Inge Bongo. Combs denied the charges.<sup id="cite_ref-People_Silverman_September_25,_1997_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-People_Silverman_September_25,_1997-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> By the late 1990s, he was being criticized for watering down and overly commercializing hip hop, and for using too many guest appearances, <a href="/wiki/Sampling_(music)" title="Sampling (music)">samples</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Interpolation_(popular_music)" title="Interpolation (popular music)">interpolations</a> of past hits in his new songs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201063_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201063-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1999.E2.80.932000:_Forever.2C_and_Club_New_York_shooting"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1999–2000:_Forever,_and_Club_New_York_shooting">1999–2000: <i>Forever</i>, and Club New York shooting</span></h3>
<p>In April 1999, Combs was charged with assaulting <a href="/wiki/Steve_Stoute" title="Steve Stoute">Steve Stoute</a> of <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>. Stoute was the manager for <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, with whom Combs had filmed a video earlier that year for the song "<a href="/wiki/Hate_Me_Now" title="Hate Me Now">Hate Me Now</a>". Combs was concerned that the video, which featured a shot of Nas and Combs being crucified, was blasphemous. He asked for his scenes on the cross to be pulled, but after the video aired unedited on MTV on April 15, Combs visited Stoute's offices and injured Stoute. Combs was charged with second-degree assault and criminal mischief,<sup id="cite_ref-Sinclair_1999_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sinclair_1999-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Allen_1999_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allen_1999-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> and was sentenced to attend a one-day anger management class.<sup id="cite_ref-Philips_1999_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philips_1999-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Forever_(Puff_Daddy_album)" title="Forever (Puff Daddy album)">Forever</a></i>, Combs' second solo studio album, was released by Bad Boy Records on August 24, 1999, in North America, and in the UK on the following day. It reached number two on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and number one on the <a href="/wiki/Top_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" title="Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums">Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums</a> chart,<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard:_Forever_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard:_Forever-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> where it remained for one week before being knocked off by Mary J. Blige's fourth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_(Mary_J._Blige_album)" title="Mary (Mary J. Blige album)">Mary</a></i>. The album received positive to mixed reviews from music critics and spawned three singles that have charted on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)"><i>Billboard</i></a> charts. It peaked at number four on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canadian Albums Chart</a>, Combs' highest-charting album in that country.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard:_Forever_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard:_Forever-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 27, 1999, Combs, his then-girlfriend <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a>, and his protégé rapper <a href="/wiki/Shyne" title="Shyne">Shyne</a> were at Club New York in <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a> in Manhattan when gunfire broke out.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> A prosecutor said that the incident was sparked by an argument at the club between Combs and another patron.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> After a police investigation, Combs and Shyne were arrested for weapons violations and other charges.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_Rashbaum_December_28,_1999_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Rashbaum_December_28,_1999-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Combs was charged with four weapons-related charges and with bribing his driver, Wardel Fenderson, to claim ownership of his gun.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_Finkelstein_Filkins_March_15,_2001_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Finkelstein_Filkins_March_15,_2001-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With a <a href="/wiki/Gag_order" title="Gag order">gag order</a> in place, the highly publicized trial began.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_Finkelstein_Filkins_March_15,_2001_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Finkelstein_Filkins_March_15,_2001-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Combs' attorneys were <a href="/wiki/Johnnie_Cochran" title="Johnnie Cochran">Johnnie L. Cochran Jr.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Brafman" title="Benjamin Brafman">Benjamin Brafman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_Finkelstein_March_17,_2001_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Finkelstein_March_17,_2001-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Combs was found not guilty on all charges; Shyne was convicted on five of his eight charges<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_Finkelstein_March_17,_2001_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Finkelstein_March_17,_2001-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and sentenced to ten years in prison. Combs and Lopez broke up shortly after. A lawsuit filed by Fenderson, who said he suffered emotional damage after the shooting, was settled in February 2004. Lawyers for both sides, having agreed to keep the settlement terms secret, said the matter had been "resolved to the satisfaction of all parties".<sup id="cite_ref-People_Silverman_February_4,_2004_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-People_Silverman_February_4,_2004-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2001.E2.80.932004:_.22P._Diddy.22_and_The_Saga_Continues"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2001–2004:_&quot;P._Diddy&quot;_and_The_Saga_Continues">2001–2004: "P. Diddy" and <i>The Saga Continues</i></span></h3>
<p>Combs changed his stage name from "Puff Daddy" to "P. Diddy" in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_March_2001_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_March_2001-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel</a> album, <i>Thank You</i>, which had been completed just before the beginning of the weapons trial, was due to be released in March that year, but remains unreleased as of October 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sean_Combs&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-6_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-6-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> He appeared as a drug dealer in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Made_(2001_film)" title="Made (2001 film)">Made</a></i> and starred with <a href="/wiki/Halle_Berry" title="Halle Berry">Halle Berry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heath_Ledger" title="Heath Ledger">Heath Ledger</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Billy_Bob_Thornton" title="Billy Bob Thornton">Billy Bob Thornton</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Monster%27s_Ball" title="Monster&#39;s Ball">Monster's Ball</a></i> (both in 2001).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He was arrested for driving with a suspended license in Florida.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_April_16,_2001_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_April_16,_2001-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Combs began working with a series of atypical (for him) artists. For a short period of time, he was the manager of <a href="/wiki/Kelis" title="Kelis">Kelis</a>; they have a collaboration titled "Let's Get Ill".<sup id="cite_ref-Amazon_Let&#39;s_Get_Ill_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amazon_Let&#39;s_Get_Ill-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> He was an opening act for <a href="/wiki/%27N_Sync" class="mw-redirect" title="&#39;N Sync">'N Sync</a> on their Spring 2002 Celebrity Tour,<sup id="cite_ref-XXL_2011_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XXL_2011-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and he signed California-based pop girl group <a href="/wiki/Dream_(American_group)" title="Dream (American group)">Dream</a> to his record label.<sup id="cite_ref-Hiatt_2001_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hiatt_2001-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Combs was a producer of the soundtrack album for the film <i><a href="/wiki/Training_Day" title="Training Day">Training Day</a></i> (2001).<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_Training_Day_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Training_Day-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2001, Combs ended Bad Boy's joint venture with Arista Records, gaining full control of Bad Boy, its catalogue, and its roster of artists.<sup id="cite_ref-Black_Profile_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Black_Profile-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Saga_Continues..." title="The Saga Continues...">The Saga Continues...</a></i>, released on July 10 in North America, was the last studio album released by the joint venture. The album reached number 2 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and the Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums charts,<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_The_Saga_Continues_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_The_Saga_Continues-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and was eventually certified Platinum.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201049_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201049-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> It is the only studio album under the P. Diddy name, and the first album by Sean Combs not to feature any guest appearances by Jay-Z or Lil Kim. Combs was executive producer of the reality TV show <i><a href="/wiki/Making_the_Band" title="Making the Band">Making the Band</a></i>, which appeared on MTV from 2002 to 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201084_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201084-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The show involves interviewing candidates and creating musical acts that would then enter the music business. Acts who got their start this way include <a href="/wiki/Da_Band" title="Da Band">Da Band</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Reid_2003_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid_2003-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Danity_Kane" title="Danity Kane">Danity Kane</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201084_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201084-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Day26" title="Day26">Day26</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_Day_26_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_Day_26-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Donnie_Klang" title="Donnie Klang">Donnie Klang</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_Donny_Klang_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_Donny_Klang-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, Combs ran in the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Marathon" title="New York City Marathon">New York City Marathon</a>, raising $2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million for the educational system of the city of New York.<sup id="cite_ref-CBS_News_November_2003_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBS_News_November_2003-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> On March 10, 2004, he appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oprah_Winfrey_Show" title="The Oprah Winfrey Show">The Oprah Winfrey Show</a></i> to discuss the marathon, which he finished in four hours and eighteen minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201089_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201089-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, Combs headed the campaign "<a href="/wiki/Vote_or_Die" class="mw-redirect" title="Vote or Die">Vote or Die</a>" for the 2004 presidential election.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201085_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201085-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> On February 1, 2004, Combs (as P. Diddy) performed at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXVIII_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl XXXVIII halftime show">Super Bowl XXXVIII halftime show</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Washington_Post_February_2004_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Washington_Post_February_2004-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2005.E2.80.932009:_.22Diddy.22_and_Press_Play"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2005–2009:_&quot;Diddy&quot;_and_Press_Play">2005–2009: "Diddy" and <i>Press Play</i></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sean_Combs.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Sean_Combs.jpg/150px-Sean_Combs.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="251" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Sean_Combs.jpg/225px-Sean_Combs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Sean_Combs.jpg/300px-Sean_Combs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="764" data-file-height="1280" /></a><figcaption>Combs performing in 2006</figcaption></figure>
<p>On August 16, 2005, Combs announced on <i><a href="/wiki/Today_(NBC_program)" class="mw-redirect" title="Today (NBC program)">Today</a></i> that he was altering his stage name yet again; he would be calling himself "Diddy". Combs said fans did not know how to address him, which led to confusion.<sup id="cite_ref-gnextinc_August_2005_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gnextinc_August_2005-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In November 2005, London-based musical artist and DJ <a href="/wiki/Diddy_(DJ)" title="Diddy (DJ)">Richard Dearlove</a>, who had been performing under the name "Diddy" since 1992&#160;&#8211;&#32; nine years before Combs started using even "P. Diddy"&#160;&#8211;&#32; sought an injunction in the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice" title="High Court of Justice">High Court of Justice</a> in London. He accepted an out-of-court settlement of £10,000 in damages and more than £100,000 in <a href="/wiki/Costs_(English_law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Costs (English law)">costs</a>. Combs can no longer use the name Diddy in the UK, where he is still known as P. Diddy.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_September_2009_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_September_2009-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_September_2006_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_September_2006-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> An assault charge against Combs filed by Michigan television host <a href="/wiki/Rogelio_Mills" title="Rogelio Mills">Rogelio Mills</a> was resolved in Combs' favor in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-contactmusic_August_2005_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-contactmusic_August_2005-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Combs starred in the 2005 film <i><a href="/wiki/Carlito%27s_Way:_Rise_to_Power" title="Carlito&#39;s Way: Rise to Power">Carlito's Way: Rise to Power</a></i>. He played Walter Lee Younger in the 2004 Broadway revival of <i><a href="/wiki/A_Raisin_in_the_Sun" title="A Raisin in the Sun">A Raisin in the Sun</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Variety_April_2004_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety_April_2004-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/A_Raisin_in_the_Sun_(2008_film)" title="A Raisin in the Sun (2008 film)">television adaptation</a> that aired in February 2008. In 2005, Combs sold half of his record company to the <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Daily_News_April_2005_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Daily_News_April_2005-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> He hosted the 2005 <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Video Music Award">MTV Video Music Awards</a> and was named one of the 100 Most Influential People of 2005 by <i><a href="/wiki/Time_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Time Magazine">Time</a></i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-Time_April_2006_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time_April_2006-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> He was mentioned in the country song "<a href="/wiki/Play_Something_Country" title="Play Something Country">Play Something Country</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Brooks_%26_Dunn" title="Brooks &amp; Dunn">Brooks &amp; Dunn</a>: the lyricist says he "didn't come to hear P. Diddy", which is rhymed with "something thumpin' from the city".<sup id="cite_ref-Cowboy_Lyrics_15929_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cowboy_Lyrics_15929-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2006, when Combs refused to release musician <a href="/wiki/Mase" title="Mase">Mase</a> from his contractual obligations to allow him to join the group <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a>, <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> recorded a <a href="/wiki/Diss_(music)" title="Diss (music)">diss</a> song, "Hip-Hop". The lyrics imply that Combs knew the identity of <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">the Notorious B.I.G.</a>'s murderer.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_September_2006_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_September_2006-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The two later resolved the feud.<sup id="cite_ref-AllHipHop_September_2006_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllHipHop_September_2006-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Combs released his first album in four years, <i><a href="/wiki/Press_Play_(album)" title="Press Play (album)">Press Play</a></i>, on October 17, 2006, on the Bad Boy Records label.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_October_2006_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_October_2006-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The album, featuring guest appearances by many popular artists, debuted at number one on the U.S. <i>Billboard</i> 200 chart<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201096_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201096-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> with sales of over 173,009. Its singles "<a href="/wiki/Come_to_Me_(Diddy_song)" title="Come to Me (Diddy song)">Come to Me</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Last_Night_(Diddy_song)" title="Last Night (Diddy song)">Last Night</a>" both reached the top ten of the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_Come_To_Me_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Come_To_Me-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_Last_Night_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Last_Night-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The album became available to preview on MTV's <i>The Leak</i> on October 10, 2006, a week before being sold in stores.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_Press_Play_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_Press_Play-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> <i>Press Play</i> received mixed to positive reviews from critics,<sup id="cite_ref-MetaCritic_Press_Play_reviews_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetaCritic_Press_Play_reviews-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and was certified Gold on the RIAA ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201049_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201049-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> On September 18, 2007, Combs teamed up with <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> for the "<a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a> I Get Money Billion Dollar Remix".<sup id="cite_ref-Hip_Hop_2007_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hip_Hop_2007-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2008, the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> claimed that the Notorious B.I.G. and Combs orchestrated the <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">1994 robbery and shooting of Tupac</a>, substantiating the claim with supposed FBI documents; the newspaper later retracted the story, acknowledging that the documents had been fabricated.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes_April_2008_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes_April_2008-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Dexter Isaac, an associate of record management executive <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Henchman" class="mw-redirect" title="Jimmy Henchman">Jimmy Henchman</a>, confessed in 2012 that he had shot Tupac on Henchman's orders.<sup id="cite_ref-Baltimore_Sun_2012_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baltimore_Sun_2012-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Philips_2012_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philips_2012-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2008, Combs' representative denied rumors of another name change.<sup id="cite_ref-nonamechange_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nonamechange-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Combs ventured into reality television in August 2008 with the premiere of his <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/I_Want_to_Work_for_Diddy" title="I Want to Work for Diddy">I Want to Work for Diddy</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-vh1.com_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vh1.com-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> He appeared—credited under his real name—in two episodes of Season 7 of <i><a href="/wiki/CSI:_Miami" title="CSI: Miami">CSI: Miami</a></i>: "Presumed Guilty" and "Sink or Swim", in the role of lawyer Derek Powell.<sup id="cite_ref-IMDb_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMDb-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2010.E2.80.932013:_Diddy_.E2.80.93_Dirty_Money_and_acting"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–2013:_Diddy_–_Dirty_Money_and_acting">2010–2013: Diddy – Dirty Money and acting</span></h3>
<p>Combs created a rap supergroup in 2010 known as the Dream Team. The group consists of Combs, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a>, <a href="/wiki/DJ_Khaled" title="DJ Khaled">DJ Khaled</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fat_Joe" title="Fat Joe">Fat Joe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Busta_Rhymes" title="Busta Rhymes">Busta Rhymes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_Caf%C3%A9" title="Red Café">Red Café</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fabolous" title="Fabolous">Fabolous</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mtv_Busta_Rhymes_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtv_Busta_Rhymes-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Combs made an appearance at comedian <a href="/wiki/Chris_Gethard" title="Chris Gethard">Chris Gethard</a>'s live show in January 2010 at the <a href="/wiki/Upright_Citizens_Brigade_Theatre" title="Upright Citizens Brigade Theatre">Upright Citizens Brigade Theatre</a> in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-Twitter_December_2009_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Twitter_December_2009-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> In June 2010, Combs played a role (credited as Sean Combs) in the comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Him_to_the_Greek" title="Get Him to the Greek">Get Him to the Greek</a></i>, as Sergio Roma, a record company executive. An <i><a href="/wiki/Entourage_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Entourage (U.S. TV series)">Entourage</a></i> series representative announced that Combs would guest star on an episode during the 2010 season.<sup id="cite_ref-TV_Guide_June_2010_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TV_Guide_June_2010-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Recruiting singers <a href="/wiki/Dawn_Richard" title="Dawn Richard">Dawn Richard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kalenna_Harper" title="Kalenna Harper">Kalenna Harper</a>, Combs formed the female duo <a href="/wiki/Diddy_%E2%80%93_Dirty_Money" title="Diddy – Dirty Money">Diddy – Dirty Money</a> in 2009. The duo's first album, <i><a href="/wiki/Last_Train_to_Paris" title="Last Train to Paris">Last Train to Paris</a></i>, was released by on December 13, 2010. The release was preceded by four singles "<a href="/wiki/Angels_(Diddy_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Angels (Diddy song)">Angels</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hello_Good_Morning" title="Hello Good Morning">Hello Good Morning</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Loving_You_No_More" title="Loving You No More">Loving You No More</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Coming_Home_(Diddy_%E2%80%93_Dirty_Money_song)" title="Coming Home (Diddy – Dirty Money song)">Coming Home</a>", which experienced mixed success on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>. "Coming Home" was the most successful of the songs, peaking at number eleven on the U.S. Hot 100, number four in the UK, and number seven in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-Allmusic_Coming_Home_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic_Coming_Home-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Combs produced the group, and often performed with them. On March 10, 2011, Diddy and Dirty Money performed "Coming Home" live on <i>American Idol</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_March_2011_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_March_2011-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 18, 2011, Combs appeared in <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_Five-0_(2010_TV_series,_season_1)" title="Hawaii Five-0 (2010 TV series, season 1)">season one</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Hawaii_Five-0_(2010_TV_series)" title="Hawaii Five-0 (2010 TV series)">Hawaii Five-0</a></i>, guest starring as an undercover <a href="/wiki/New_York_Police_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Police Department">NYPD</a> detective.<sup id="cite_ref-Okita_2011_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Okita_2011-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In November 2012 Combs appeared in an episode of the <a href="/wiki/It%27s_Always_Sunny_in_Philadelphia_(season_8)" title="It&#39;s Always Sunny in Philadelphia (season 8)">eighth season</a> of the American sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_Always_Sunny_in_Philadelphia" title="It&#39;s Always Sunny in Philadelphia">It's Always Sunny in Philadelphia</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Couch_2012_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Couch_2012-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2014.E2.80.93present:_MMM_.28Money_Making_Mitch.29.2C_No_Way_Out_2.2C_and_The_Love_Album:_Off_the_Grid"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–present:_MMM_(Money_Making_Mitch),_No_Way_Out_2,_and_The_Love_Album:_Off_the_Grid">2014–present: <i>MMM (Money Making Mitch)</i>, <i>No Way Out 2</i>, and <i>The Love Album: Off the Grid</i></span></h3>
<p>On February 26, 2014, Combs premiered "Big Homie", featuring Rick Ross and <a href="/wiki/French_Montana" title="French Montana">French Montana</a>, as the first single from his mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/MMM_(Money_Making_Mitch)" title="MMM (Money Making Mitch)">MMM (Money Making Mitch)</a></i>, which was originally scheduled to be released that year.<sup id="cite_ref-Ortiz_2014_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ortiz_2014-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The song was released for digital download on March 24,<sup id="cite_ref-iTunes_March_2014_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iTunes_March_2014-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> and two days later the trailer for the music video was released. The full version of the music video was released on March 31. Combs used his former stage name Puff Daddy for the album.<sup id="cite_ref-XXL_March_25,_2014_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XXL_March_25,_2014-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> <i>MMM</i> was released as a free mixtape album of 12 tracks on November 4, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Reed_November_2015_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reed_November_2015-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> In 2014 Combs and <a href="/wiki/Guy_Gerber" title="Guy Gerber">Guy Gerber</a> announced that their joint album <i>11 11</i> would be available for free download.<sup id="cite_ref-Guy_Gerber_&amp;_Puff_Daddy_Present_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guy_Gerber_&amp;_Puff_Daddy_Present-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> A new single called "<a href="/wiki/Finna_Get_Loose" title="Finna Get Loose">Finna Get Loose</a>" featuring Combs and <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a> was released on June 29, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Reed_June_2015_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reed_June_2015-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2015, Bad Boy Entertainment artist Gizzle told the press that she is collaborating with Combs on what she describes as his last album, titled <i>No Way Out 2</i>, a sequel to his 1997 debut. She describes the music as unique: "The mindset is to just be classic and to be epic. And to really live up to that<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... we know it's a tall order, but we welcome the challenge."<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-7_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-7-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> In April 2016, Combs announced that after this last album and tour, he plans to retire from the music industry to focus on acting.<sup id="cite_ref-Rayne_2016_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rayne_2016-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 20 and 21, 2016, Combs launched a tour of <a href="/wiki/Bad_Boy_Records" title="Bad Boy Records">Bad Boy Records</a>' biggest names to celebrate the 20th anniversary of the label.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-8_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-8-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The documentary <i>Can't Stop, Won't Stop: A Bad Boy Story</i>, covering the two shows at the <a href="/wiki/Barclays_Center" title="Barclays Center">Barclays Center</a> in Brooklyn as well as behind-the-scenes events, was released on June 23, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-9_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-9-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The show toured to an additional twenty venues across the United States and Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-10_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-10-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-11_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-11-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 5, 2017, Combs announced that he would be going by the name Love, stating "My new name is Love, aka Brother Love".<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-12_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-12-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Two days later, he told the press he had been joking, but on January 3, 2018, he announced on <i><a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Kimmel_Live!" title="Jimmy Kimmel Live!">Jimmy Kimmel Live!</a></i> that he had changed his mind again, and will be using the new name after all.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-13_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-13-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The change became official in 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019, Combs announced on Twitter that <i>Making the Band</i> would return to MTV in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-14_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-14-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Combs executive-produced Nigerian singer <a href="/wiki/Burna_Boy" title="Burna Boy">Burna Boy</a>'s album, <i><a href="/wiki/Twice_as_Tall" title="Twice as Tall">Twice as Tall</a></i>, released on August 14, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2022, Combs hosted the <a href="/wiki/2022_Billboard_Music_Awards" title="2022 Billboard Music Awards">2022 <i>Billboard</i> Music Awards</a>. Shortly afterwards, he announced the startup of a new record label, Love Records as a one-album recording deal with <a href="/wiki/Motown" title="Motown">Motown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 22, 2023, Combs released a teaser trailer on social media for his sixth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Love_Album:_Off_the_Grid" title="The Love Album: Off the Grid">The Love Album: Off the Grid</a></i>, which was released on September 15, 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_career">Business career</span></h2>
<p><i>Fortune</i> magazine listed Combs at number twelve on their <a href="/wiki/40_under_40_(Fortune_Magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="40 under 40 (Fortune Magazine)">top 40 of entrepreneurs under 40</a> in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-Halifaxlive_February_2005_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halifaxlive_February_2005-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> Magazine estimated that for the year ending May 2017, Combs earned $130 million, ranking him number one among entertainers.<sup id="cite_ref-Robehmed_2017_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robehmed_2017-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> In 2022, his estimated net worth was US$1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sean_John">Sean John</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Broadway_Crowds_(5896264776)_crop.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Broadway_Crowds_%285896264776%29_crop.jpg/220px-Broadway_Crowds_%285896264776%29_crop.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Broadway_Crowds_%285896264776%29_crop.jpg/330px-Broadway_Crowds_%285896264776%29_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Broadway_Crowds_%285896264776%29_crop.jpg/440px-Broadway_Crowds_%285896264776%29_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3799" data-file-height="2581" /></a><figcaption>A billboard of Sean John is in the distance on <a href="/wiki/Broadway_(Manhattan)" title="Broadway (Manhattan)">Broadway</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1998, Combs started a clothing line, <i><a href="/wiki/Sean_John" title="Sean John">Sean John</a></i>. It was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Fashion_Designers_of_America" title="Council of Fashion Designers of America">Council of Fashion Designers of America</a> (CFDA) award for Menswear Designer of the Year in 2000,<sup id="cite_ref-LookOnline_2000_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LookOnline_2000-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> and won in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-CFDA_2012_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CFDA_2012-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> California billionaire <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Burkle" title="Ronald Burkle">Ronald Burkle</a> invested $100 million into the company in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-15_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-15-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Also in 2003, the <a href="/wiki/National_Labor_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="National Labor Committee">National Labor Committee</a> revealed that factories producing the clothing in Honduras were violating Honduran labor laws.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_PDF_October_2003_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_PDF_October_2003-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Among the accusations were that workers were subjected to body searches and involuntary pregnancy tests. Bathrooms were locked and access tightly controlled. Employees were forced to work overtime and were paid sweatshop wages.<sup id="cite_ref-Democracynow_December_2003_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Democracynow_December_2003-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Kernaghan" title="Charles Kernaghan">Charles Kernaghan</a> of the National Labor Committee told <i>The New York Times</i> that "Sean Puff Daddy obviously has a lot of clout, he can literally do a lot overnight to help these workers."<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_PDF_October_2003_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_PDF_October_2003-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Combs responded with an extensive investigation, telling reporters "I'm as pro-worker as they get".<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_October_2003_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_October_2003-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> On February 14, 2004, Kernaghan announced that improvements had been implemented at the factory, including adding air conditioning and water purification systems, firing the most abusive supervisors, and allowing the formation of a labor union.<sup id="cite_ref-NLCnet_December_2003_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NLCnet_December_2003-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> In late 2006, the department store <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy&#39;s">Macy's</a> removed Sean John jackets from their shelves when they discovered that the clothing was made using <a href="/wiki/Raccoon_dog" class="mw-redirect" title="Raccoon dog">raccoon dog</a> fur. Combs had not known the jackets were made with genuine fur, but as soon as he was alerted, he had production stopped.<sup id="cite_ref-MSNBC_December_2006_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC_December_2006-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2008, Combs added a men's perfume called "I Am King" to the Sean John brand. The fragrance, dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali" title="Muhammad Ali">Muhammad Ali</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_Jr." title="Martin Luther King Jr.">Martin Luther King Jr.</a>, featured model <a href="/wiki/Bar_Refaeli" title="Bar Refaeli">Bar Refaeli</a> in its advertisements.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201082_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201082-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> In early 2016, Sean John introduced the brand's GIRLS collection.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-16_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-16-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ventures">Other ventures</span></h3>
<p>Combs is the head of Combs Enterprises, an umbrella company for his portfolio of businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-17_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-17-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> In addition to his clothing line, Combs owned two restaurants called Justin's, named after his son. The original New York location closed in September 2007;<sup id="cite_ref-Ugwu_2011_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ugwu_2011-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> the Atlanta location closed in June 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolfe_2012_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolfe_2012-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> He is the designer of the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Mavericks" title="Dallas Mavericks">Dallas Mavericks</a> alternate jersey.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_December_2003_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_December_2003-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> In October 2007, Combs agreed to help develop the <a href="/wiki/C%C3%AEroc" title="Cîroc">Cîroc</a> vodka brand for a 50 percent share of the profits.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201082_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201082-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Combs acquired the <a href="/wiki/Enyce" title="Enyce">Enyce</a> clothing line from <a href="/wiki/Liz_Claiborne" title="Liz Claiborne">Liz Claiborne</a> for $20 million on October 21, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Vibe_October_2008_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vibe_October_2008-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Combs has a major equity stake in <a href="/wiki/Revolt_(TV_network)" title="Revolt (TV network)">Revolt TV</a>, a television network that also has a film production branch.<sup id="cite_ref-Finke_2012_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Finke_2012-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> It began broadcasting in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Greenburg_2014_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenburg_2014-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In February 2015, Combs teamed up with actor <a href="/wiki/Mark_Wahlberg" title="Mark Wahlberg">Mark Wahlberg</a> and businessman <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Burkle" title="Ronald Burkle">Ronald Burkle</a> of <a href="/wiki/Yucaipa_Companies" title="Yucaipa Companies">Yucaipa Companies</a> to purchase a majority holding in Aquahydrate, a calorie-free beverage for athletes.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-19_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-19-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-20_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-20-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> John Cochran, former president of <a href="/wiki/Fiji_Water" title="Fiji Water">Fiji Water</a>, is CEO of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-21_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-21-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019, Combs became a major investor in PlayVS, which provides an infrastructure for competitive gaming in US high schools.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> The company was also backed by <a href="/wiki/Twitch_(service)" title="Twitch (service)">Twitch</a> co-founder Kevin Lin.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sean_Combs_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Sean_Combs_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/220px-Sean_Combs_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="241" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Sean_Combs_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/330px-Sean_Combs_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Sean_Combs_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/440px-Sean_Combs_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2144" data-file-height="2351" /></a><figcaption>Combs with his sons Christian and Justin at the <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_3" title="Spider-Man 3">Spider-Man 3</a></i> premiere (2007)</figcaption></figure>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family">Family</span></h3>
<p>Combs is the father of 7 children. His first biological child, Justin, was born in 1993 to designer <a href="/wiki/Misa_Hylton" title="Misa Hylton">Misa Hylton-Brim</a>. Justin attended <a href="/wiki/UCLA" class="mw-redirect" title="UCLA">UCLA</a> on a football scholarship.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes_Mather_June_1,_2012_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes_Mather_June_1,_2012-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Combs had an on-again, off-again relationship with Kimberly Porter (1970–2018), which lasted from 1994 to 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-USA_Today_2007_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USA_Today_2007-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201080_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201080-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> He raised and adopted <a href="/wiki/Quincy_(actor)" title="Quincy (actor)">Quincy</a> (born 1991),<sup id="cite_ref-Essence_2009_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Essence_2009-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Porter's son from a previous relationship with singer-producer <a href="/wiki/Al_B._Sure!" title="Al B. Sure!">Al B. Sure!</a> Together they had a son, Christian (born 1998), and twin daughters, D'Lila Star and Jessie James (born 2006).<sup id="cite_ref-Silverman_2007_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Silverman_2007-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Porter died of <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a> on November 15, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-22_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-22-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-23_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-23-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Five months before the birth of his twins,<sup id="cite_ref-Silverman_2007_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Silverman_2007-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Combs' daughter Chance was born to Sarah Chapman. He took legal responsibility for Chance in October 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201080_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201080-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Combs was in a long-term relationship with <a href="/wiki/Cassie_Ventura" title="Cassie Ventura">Cassie Ventura</a> from 2007 to 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-3_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-3-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-4_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-4-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Combs' sons Quincy and Justin both appeared on MTV's <i><a href="/wiki/My_Super_Sweet_16" title="My Super Sweet 16">My Super Sweet 16</a></i>. Combs threw Quincy a celebrity-studded party and gave him two cars as his 16th birthday present.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_Quincy_Sweet_Sixteen_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_Quincy_Sweet_Sixteen-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Birthday_Fab_2007_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Birthday_Fab_2007-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> For Justin's 16th birthday, Combs presented him with a $360,000 <a href="/wiki/Maybach" title="Maybach">Maybach</a> car.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes_Mather_June_1,_2012_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes_Mather_June_1,_2012-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Justin_Sweet_16_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Justin_Sweet_16-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His seventh child was born on October 15, 2022, a daughter named Love Sean Combs.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> The mother is Dana Tran.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2022, Diddy and son Christian became the first father-son duo to have simultaneous #1 hits. Diddy reached the top of the <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_charts" title="Billboard charts">Billboard</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Adult_R%26B_Songs" title="Adult R&amp;B Songs">Adult R&amp;B Airplay</a> chart with "Gotta Move On," while Christian, under his stage name King Combs, topped <a href="/wiki/Mediabase" title="Mediabase">Mediabase</a>'s US Urban Radio chart with "Can't Stop Won't Stop," featuring <a href="/wiki/Kodak_Black" title="Kodak Black">Kodak Black</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-father-son_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-father-son-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Combs owns a home in <a href="/wiki/Alpine,_New_Jersey" title="Alpine, New Jersey">Alpine, New Jersey</a>, which he purchased for $7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_Century_February_11,_2007_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Century_February_11,_2007-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charity_work_and_honors">Charity work and honors</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sean_Diddy_Combs_Hollywood_Star.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Sean_Diddy_Combs_Hollywood_Star.jpg/220px-Sean_Diddy_Combs_Hollywood_Star.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Sean_Diddy_Combs_Hollywood_Star.jpg/330px-Sean_Diddy_Combs_Hollywood_Star.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Sean_Diddy_Combs_Hollywood_Star.jpg/440px-Sean_Diddy_Combs_Hollywood_Star.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a><figcaption>Combs' star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Combs founded Daddy's House Social Programs, an organization to help inner city youth, in 1995. Programs include tutoring, life skills classes, and an annual summer camp. Along with Jay-Z, he pledged $1 million to help support victims of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> in 2005, and donated clothing from his Sean John line to victims. He has donated computers and books to New York schools.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETraugh201088_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETraugh201088-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1998, he received a Golden Plate Award from the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Achievement" title="Academy of Achievement">American Academy of Achievement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Chicago Mayor <a href="/wiki/Richard_M._Daley" title="Richard M. Daley">Richard M. Daley</a> named October 13, 2006, as "Diddy Day" in honor of Combs' charity work.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones201494_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones201494-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, Combs was honored with a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Today_MSNBC_May_2008_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Today_MSNBC_May_2008-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> the first male rapper to be so honored.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, Combs received an <a href="/wiki/Honorary_doctorate" class="mw-redirect" title="Honorary doctorate">honorary doctorate</a> from <a href="/wiki/Howard_University" title="Howard University">Howard University</a>, where he gave the <a href="/wiki/Commencement_speech" title="Commencement speech">commencement speech</a> for its 146th commencement ceremony. In his speech, Combs acknowledged that his experiences as a Howard student positively influenced his life.<sup id="cite_ref-Aratani_2014_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aratani_2014-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, Combs donated $1 million to Howard University to establish the Sean Combs Scholarship Fund to help students who are unable to pay their tuition.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoRQ-24_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoRQ-24-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2022, Combs announced during his <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards_2022" title="BET Awards 2022">BET Lifetime Achievement Award</a> acceptance speech that he will be donating $1 million each to Howard University and <a href="/wiki/Jackson_State_University" title="Jackson State University">Jackson State University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wardrobe_style">Wardrobe style</span></h3>
<p>Combs describes his wardrobe style as "swagger, timeless, diverse".<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_2010_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph_2010-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> On September 2, 2007, Combs held his ninth annual "White Party", at which guests are limited to an all-white dress code. The White Party, which has also been held in <a href="/wiki/St._Tropez" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Tropez">St. Tropez</a>, was held in his home in <a href="/wiki/East_Hampton_(town),_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="East Hampton (town), New York">East Hampton, New York</a>. Combs stated, "This party is up there with the top three that I've thrown. It's a party that has legendary status. It's hard to throw a party that lives up to its legend."<sup id="cite_ref-AOL_September_2007_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AOL_September_2007-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_views">Religious views</span></h3>
<p>Combs was raised <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a>, and was an altar server as a boy.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, he told <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> that he does not adhere to any specific religious denomination. He said, "I just follow right from wrong, so I could pray in a synagogue or a mosque or a church. I believe that there is only one God."<sup id="cite_ref-:0_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 3, 2020, Combs invited his Twitter followers to view a 3-hour YouTube video posted by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Farrakhan" title="Louis Farrakhan">Louis Farrakhan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> In the video Farrakhan made multiple comments and repeatedly used the phrase "<a href="/wiki/Synagogue_of_Satan" title="Synagogue of Satan">Synagogue of Satan</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> The video was removed from YouTube for violating its policy against hate speech.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In response to comedian <a href="/wiki/Nick_Cannon" title="Nick Cannon">Nick Cannon</a> being fired on July 14, 2020, from <a href="/wiki/ViacomCBS" class="mw-redirect" title="ViacomCBS">ViacomCBS</a> for espousing anti-Semitic views,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Combs tweeted that Cannon should "come home to RevoltTv" saying "We got your back and love you and what you have done for the culture."<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_awards">Other awards</span></h3>
<p>In 2021, Combs was among the inaugural inductees into the <a href="/wiki/Black_Music_and_Entertainment_Walk_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Music and Entertainment Walk of Fame">Black Music and Entertainment Walk of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2022, Combs received the <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards#Special_awards" title="BET Awards">BET Lifetime Achievement Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
